      2. By His death and resurrection, He accomplished this redemption and became our Savior.
    2. Call upon the name of the Lord
      1. According to our thought, because we have neither seen Him nor touched Him it is difficult to call on the Lord’s name.
      2. In reality it is easy. We do not need to see or touch Him; once we have heard of His name, we can just call.
      3. To call on the name of the Lord is just to call on the Lord Himself.
      4. To call on the name of the Lord is also to believe in the Lord. Romans 10:14 says, “How then shall they call upon Him in Whom they have not believed?” Therefore, calling includes believing.
      5. Believing includes repentance. “Repentance” means to turn our minds to God, confessing our sins.
    3. Whosoever calls shall be saved
      1. To call is to believe; therefore, calling results in immediate salvation.
      2. When we call upon the Lord, the Holy Spirit brings God and His salvation to us. This proves that once we call, we are saved.
      3. The fact of our receiving this salvation is not based upon our feeling. If it seems that you have not received after calling, this is simply your feeling. In reality you have received because the Word says, “Whosoever calls upon the name of the Lord shall be saved.”
    4. The meaning of being saved
      1. To be saved means to receive forgiveness of sins.
      2. To be saved also means to receive the life of God.

    Subject One Hundred Fifty-nine

    THE WORD OF THE CROSS

    Scripture: 1 Cor. 1:18-21

    1. The meaning of the cross
      1. The cross is both the instrument by which the Lord Jesus died and the place where He died.
      2. By His death on the cross the Lord Jesus bore the sins of mankind and saved man from destruction.
      3. Therefore, the cross is able to deliver man from sin and destruction.
    2. The word of the cross
      1. The word of the cross includes the meaning of the cross and the teaching of the cross.
      2. Those who regard the meaning and the teaching of the cross as foolishness will perish. Those who receive the word of the cross, recognizing that it is the power of God, will be saved.
      3. The reason that the meaning and the teaching of the cross can cause man to be saved is that the cross is God’s wisdom and power. Wisdom is God’s means; power is God’s ability. God’s means and ability to save man depend upon the cross.
    3. How to apply the word of the cross
      1. Confess that we have sinned and deserve to perish.
      2. Acknowledge that the cross is God’s way of salvation.
      3. Accept Jesus Christ as the Savior who died on the cross to bear our sins.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty

    CHRIST CRUCIFIED

    Scripture: 1 Cor. 1:23

    1. Who is Christ?
      1. He is the Son of God and also God Himself.
      2. He came to be a man whose name is Jesus.
      3. He came as a man in order to be our Savior.
    2. Why was Christ crucified?
      1. He was crucified in order to accomplish God’s way of salvation.
      2. He was crucified to remove the sins of man.
      3. He was crucified in order to release His life.
    3. Christ crucified
      1. Christ is the Savior; the cross is the means of salvation. Therefore, Christ crucified is the Savior who accomplished the way of salvation.
      2. Although He was Christ crucified, today He is Christ resurrected! He is no longer on the cross. He is not only the Savior who accomplished the way of salvation, but He is living to impart His saving life into man.
    4. How to receive Christ
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty-one

    JESUS IS LORD

    Scripture: 1 Cor. 12:3

    1. There is a lord of all things
      1. Everything has its lord.
      2. Who is the Lord of this great universe and the things therein?
      3. Who is your lord? Neither your parents, your husband, nor your wife is your lord. If you think they are, who will you belong to once they die? You will be a man without a lord.
    2. The creator of all things
      1. The universe and all creation has its creator.
      2. Man also has a creator.
      3. The one who created all is the Lord of all. Since all things were created by Him, all things belong to Him. He is the Lord of all.
    3. The ruler of all things
      1. There is a ruler in creation.
      2. There is a ruler over man and within man’s heart.
      3. This ruler is the Lord.
    4. The redeemer of all things
      1. Man needs redemption because he has sinned.
      2. The whole creation also needs redemption because it was corrupted through man’s sin. This is clearly seen in the Bible.
      3. The redeemer of all is the Lord of all.
    5. Jesus is Lord
      1. Jesus is the creator and the Lord of all.
      2. Jesus is the ruler of creation; as ruler, He is the Lord of all.
      3. Jesus is the redeemer of all creation; as the redeemer, He is the Lord of all.
    6. How to receive Jesus as Lord
      1. Confess that you are created, ruled, and redeemed by Him.
      2. Repent, confess your sins, and receive Him as your Savior.
      3. Acknowledge that all that you are and have belong to Him, and that He is your Lord.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty-two

    FOR WHAT DID CHRIST DIE?

    Scripture: 1 Cor. 15:3-4

    1. Presumptions of the people regarding Christ’s death
      1. The Jews said that He died because He was sentenced to death by the Roman officials.
      2. The Gentiles throughout the ages said that He sacrificed Himself for a cause.
    2. Christ’s own explanation
      1. He willingly gave His own life, to die (John 10:11, 18).
      2. He died to redeem men from their sins (Matt. 26:28).
    3. The Bible’s explanation
      1. God predestined Him to die.
      2. He was destined to die for the sins of man.
    4. The witness of the saints
      1. They confessed that Christ died for their sins, thus receiving the peace of being forgiven.
      2. This confession resulted in a change in that they no longer lived a life of sin.
    5. How to deal with Christ’s death
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty-three

    THE STING OF DEATH

    Scripture: 1 Cor. 15:55-56

    1. The fearfulness of death
      1. The most fearsome word in the dictionary is “death.”
      2. The most frightening sound is the sound of the word “death.”
      3. Death is the most frightful thing in a man’s life. Who is not afraid of death?
    2. The power of death
      1. There is no power among men that is greater than the power of death.
      2. No one can reject the visitation of death.
      3. The fact that no one is spared from death speaks of the powerfulness of death.
    3. The sting of death
      1. Death possesses man not directly, but in an indirect way.
      2. Death possesses man through sin. Sin is the sting of death. Everyone who fishes knows that one fishes with a hook. Once the fish is hooked, it is caught. Just as man fishes by using a hook, so death possesses man by sin.
      3. Sin is the sting because it is poisonous. Once sin poisons man, it possesses him. The result of sin is death. Because sin is poisonous, it deadens.
    4. How to be spared from death
      1. One needs to be freed from sin in order to be spared from death.
      2. To be freed from sin one must first believe in the Lord. On one hand the Lord died and shed His blood that we might be spared from the punishment of sin. On the other hand, He resurrected that we might be delivered from the power of sin.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty-four

    “ONE DIED FOR ALL”

    Scripture: 2 Cor. 5:14

    1. The One is Jesus
      1. Jesus is God coming to be the Savior of mankind.
      2. Since He is God incarnated, He is an unlimited person.
      3. In God’s eyes, all who believe in Jesus are included in Jesus. So Jesus is not only an unlimited person, but One that includes all.
    2. All are sinners
      1. All the people in the world are sinners.
      2. Every sinner that believes in the Lord Jesus is included in this “all.”
    3. One died for all
      1. Apparently Jesus died as one individual, yet actually He died for all. That is, He died for those He redeemed, for all those who believe in Him.
      2. The reason that the Lord’s death could become effective for all who believe in Him is that He is one with them and they are joined unto Him.
    4. All died
      1. “All” refers to all those who are joined unto Christ Jesus. Since He died, all have died in God’s sight. It is best to use the example of a nation destroyed.
      2. Since all died because of His death, “all” do not need to die again.
    5. How to share in Jesus’ death
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty-five

    THE SINLESS ONE MADE SIN

    Scripture: 2 Cor. 5:21

    1. The sinless One is Jesus
      1. Jesus as God incarnated, does not have a sinful nature.
      2. Jesus never sinned, even when He was judged. All the examinations of men could not find any sins in Jesus. Even He Himself said, “Which one of you convicts me of sin?” (John 8:46).
    2. We are sin
      1. We were born in sin.
      2. We grew up in sin.
      3. We are living in sin.
      4. We live out sin.
      5. We both possess a sinful nature and commit sinful acts, so we are sin.
    3. The sinless One became sin
      1. God caused Jesus to be our substitute. He caused the sinless Lord Jesus to replace us, who are sin, by becoming sin for us.
      2. God caused the Lord Jesus to become sin in order that He might receive God’s righteous judgment on the cross for us.
      3. When God judged the Lord Jesus, He actually judged us. By terminating the body of Jesus, He terminated us.
      4. Jesus could become sin for us because He became a man in order to be united with man.
    4. The result of His becoming sin
      1. He became sin for us that we might become righteousness.
      2. We are sin and Jesus is righteousness. When He caused us to be righteousness, He caused us to become Him.
      3. He caused us to become Him means that we may be joined to Him. Here “in Him” refers to this joining.
      4. This righteousness of His is not only before man but also before God. Not only does it fulfill the requirement and standard of man, but also that of God. Therefore, His righteousness is God’s righteousness. So when He became sin for us, He caused us to be joined with Him and in Him to become righteousness before God.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty-six

    THE SACRIFICE OF LOVE

    Scripture: Gal. 2:20

    1. The love of Christ
      1. Christ loved us, so He left heaven and the throne to be born in this world as a lowly person.
      2. Christ loved us, so He passed through thirty-three years of human sufferings.
      3. Christ loved us, so He gave Himself up at the cross; that is, He gave up His life through death.
      4. Very few lay down their lives for others, although some might die for a good man, or friends. Yet Christ laid down His life for us, even though we were His enemies. This love is a surpassing love (Rom. 5:7-8, 10).
    2. The intention of Christ’s sacrifice
      1. Not only to suffer and die for us, but to take away our sins and redeem us.
      2. Not only to satisfy our need, but to fulfill God’s requirement.
      3. Not only to make us complete, but to accomplish God’s means of salvation.
      4. His sacrifice was that we might partake of God and all He has.
    3. How to receive the love of Christ
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty-seven

    CHRIST BECAME A CURSE FOR US

    Scripture: Gal. 3:13

    1. The origin of the curse
      1. The curse came from sin.
      2. God brought in the curse after Adam sinned. God said, “Cursed is the ground for thy sake” (Gen. 3:17).
    2. The sign of the curse
      1. The sign of the curse is thorns. After Adam sinned, the earth brought forth thorns because of the curse. So thorns are the sign of being cursed.
      2. The outstanding feature of thorns is that they prick, causing pain.
    3. The execution of the curse
      1. The curse is carried out through the law. The law administers the curse. Once man sinned, God’s law then administered the curse upon man.
      2. Therefore, the curse is related to the law of God, and is the demand of the righteousness of God upon sinners.
    4. The nullification of the curse
      1. When Christ bore our sins, He also took our curse. Since the problem of sin is resolved, so is the problem of the curse.
      2. When Christ bore our sins on the cross, He wore a crown of thorns. Since the thorns are a sign of the curse, this shows that He took our curse on the cross.
      3. Since Christ was cursed in our stead on the cross, the demand of the law was fulfilled and He could redeem us from the curse of the law.
    5. How to have the curse removed
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty-eight

    CHRIST HAS SET US FREE

    Scripture: Gal. 5:1

    1. Our bondage
      1. We are under the bondage of sin.
      2. We are under the bondage of the law.
      3. We are under the bondage of Satan.
      4. We are under the bondage of death.
    2. Christ’s setting free
      1. Christ dealt with sin for us.
      2. Christ satisfied the law for us.
      3. Christ destroyed Satan for us.
      4. Christ eliminated death for us.
    3. The purpose of salvation
      1. To forgive our sins and deliver us from sin.
      2. To deliver us from the law.
      3. To deliver us from Satan’s dominion.
      4. To deliver us from the power of death.
    4. How to be released
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Sixty-nine

    REDEMPTION BY THE BLOOD

    Scripture: Eph. 1:7

    1. The result of sin
      1. Sin causes us to be under God’s condemnation.
      2. Condemnation creates a distance and a barrier between us and God.
    2. The demand of the law
      1. The law represents God’s righteousness, making absolute demands on man.
      2. The demand of the law confines the sinner under condemnation.
    3. The redemption by the blood
      1. Christ bore our sins to fulfill the demand of the law. Therefore, the blood of Christ is able to redeem us from under the law that the law could no longer confine us under condemnation.
      2. Since the blood of Christ redeems us from the condemnation of the law, it also abolishes the distance between us and God; thus, we are brought back to God. As sin and the law cause us to depart from God and become distant from Him, so the blood of Christ redeems us from under the law that we may return to God without anything between us and Him.
    4. The result of redemption
      1. Our sins are forgiven.
      2. We are brought back to God.
    5. The accomplishment of redemption is through God’s grace
    6. How to obtain redemption
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy

    DEAD IN SINS

    Scripture: Eph. 2:1

    1. The meaning of death
      1. Death means the loss of function; spiritually, this is the inability to do good.
      2. Death also means the loss of feeling; spiritually, this is the unconsciousness of sin.
    2. The fact of death
      1. The condition of man today is altogether one of death. He is unable to do good and is without the consciousness of sin. Having lost his function and feeling, he is ungodly toward God and unrighteous toward man; he is without the strength to be godly or righteous.
      2. Illustrate the facts of death. Show the inability to do good and the lack of consciousness of sin.
    3. The source of death
      1. Death comes from sin.
      2. All who sin abide in death.
    4. The result of death
      1. The death of the spirit occurs first.
      2. The death of the spirit results in the death of the body.
      3. It also causes the soul to suffer in Hades.
      4. In the end it will cause the whole being to be cast with its body, soul, and spirit into the lake of fire to suffer the second death, that is, eternal suffering.
    5. How to be free from death
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy-one

    THE SURPASSING SALVATION

    Scripture: Eph. 2:4-8

    1. The source of salvation
      1. The source of salvation is God.
      2. The source of salvation is God’s mercy.
      3. The source of salvation is God’s great love.
    2. The accomplishment of salvation
      1. Salvation is accomplished through the death and resurrection of Christ.
      2. Salvation is also accomplished through the ascension of Christ.
    3. The surpassing salvation
      1. When we were dead in sin, God’s surpassing salvation caused us to become alive together with Christ.
      2. He also caused us to be raised together with Christ. There is a difference between being made alive and being raised. To be made alive means to have life; to be raised means not only to have life but to be able to move. Not only was Lazarus enlivened in the tomb, but his coming out of the tomb shows that he was resurrected, that he was raised up.
      3. Thirdly, He caused us to sit together with Him in heavenly places. This is surpassing! This is God’s surpassing salvation.
    4. The manifestation of salvation
      1. This salvation manifests the rich and abundant grace of God.
      2. This grace is given to us in God’s kindness.
        1. Emphasize that grace is God’s action in freely saving us.
        2. Emphasize that kindness issues out of God’s mercy and love, out of the intent of His heart.
    5. How to receive this salvation
      Stress the matter of faith.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy-two

    SAVED BY GRACE

    Scripture: Eph. 2:8-9

    1. The meaning of salvation
      1. Salvation means to be forgiven and delivered from sin.
      2. Furthermore, salvation means to receive life and be resurrected.
      3. Salvation also includes being ascended and transcended.
    2. The source of salvation
      1. The grace of God is the source of salvation.
      2. Grace comes from love. Grace is an active issue, and love is an intention of the heart. So the act of grace is an issue coming from the loving intention of the heart.
      3. Because grace is free, salvation is not by works.
      4. Since it is by grace and not by works, salvation is out of God and not out of ourselves.
    3. The means of salvation
      1. Salvation is not by works, but by faith.
      2. Grace is the dispensing; faith is the receiving. The dispensing grace and the receiving faith make salvation complete.
    4. The result of salvation
      1. That man may not boast in himself. Since salvation is not by the works of man, nor out of man, there is no room for man to boast.
      2. That God may be man’s boast and glory.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy-three

    THE HUMAN LIFE HAS NO HOPE

    Scripture: Eph. 2:12

    1. The situation of man
      1. Describe how man is born, raised up, encounters sicknesses, and dies. The human life can never depart from these four things: birth, aging, sickness, and death.
      2. Conclude that everything is vanity.
    2. The hopelessness of the human life
      1. Use further examples to illustrate that once a man dies, that is the end of everything for him.
      2. Conclude that the human life is hopeless.
    3. The reason for hopelessness
      1. The reason why the human life is hopeless is that man has lost God. Without God there is no hope.
      2. God wants to be everything to the human life. Only when man has God will there be hope for his life.
    4. How to have hope
      1. Do not ignore the sense of emptiness. The sense of emptiness tells you that you need God, Who is the hope of life.
      2. Recognize that God can be everything to the human life.
      3. Repent and turn to God.
      4. Receive the Son of God, Jesus Christ. To have the Son of God is the way to have God. Once man has God, his life will be full of hope.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy-four

    THE EXCELLENCY
    OF THE KNOWLEDGE OF CHRIST

    Scripture: Phil. 3:7-9

    1. The futility of everything
      1. Point out that nothing in the universe is really a gain to man.
      2. Give concrete examples to show this. For example: education, money, and family, etc., may not be gains to man. Sometimes the more money a man has, the more harm it does. When you mention the futility of everything, bring in the subject of sickness and death. Whether one has education, money, or friendship, this cannot be escaped; whether it be parents, wife, children, or others, none can keep sickness and death away. When death comes, everything is over.
      3. Conclude that everything is vain and futile.
    2. All things are as dung
      1. As far as knowing Christ is concerned, all things are of no avail. So the nature and value of all things are as dung.
      2. Dung is a changed form of food. Parents, children, reputation, and position are all forms of food, but eventually they become dung. Everything in the world changes, and when it changes it becomes dung.
      3. Dung is the most useless and valueless of all things.
    3. The Most Excellent One in the universe
      1. Everything in the universe is vain and futile, without weight or value. Only Christ is the Most Excellent One.
      2. Christ is the embodiment of God. God is the center of the universe; He is also the reality of the universe. Hence, God is the true value of the whole universe. Because Christ is the embodiment of God, He is the Most Excellent One.
    4. To know Christ
      1. Since Christ is the Most Excellent One, to know Him is the most excellent of all things.
      2. All forms of knowledge are vain; they only add sorrow to man. Only the knowledge of Christ is real and solid, and only this will give man real happiness. So the knowledge of Christ is the most excellent thing.
    5. The result of the knowledge of Christ
      1. Not only will the knowledge of Christ give you the Most Excellent One of the universe, but it will also give you the righteousness of God. In Christ your sins will be forgiven and you will be accepted by God.
      2. In Christ you will also obtain the life of God.
    6. How to know Christ
      1. Recognize that everything is futile, that it is nothing but refuse.
      2. Despise and forsake all the vain and futile things.
      3. Receive Christ as your life and Savior.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy-five

    THE PEACE OF THE CROSS

    Scripture: Col. 1:20

    1. The problem in the universe
      1. The biggest problem in the universe is disharmony among all the creatures. Everything in the universe has this problem with God.
      2. The reason the creatures are in disharmony with God is that man is in disharmony with God. This is due to man’s sin. For example, mosquitoes and insects bite, and animals kill each other. This is all because man is out of harmony with God, which is the result of man’s sin. When sin came in, the whole universe became full of chaos.
    2. The peace of the universe
      1. The universe is out of harmony because of man’s sin. Therefore, before the universe can have peace, man’s sin must be removed.
      2. Man’s sin was removed when Christ shed His blood on the cross. Thus, through the shedding of His blood, Christ made peace in the universe.
    3. The function of the peace of the cross
      1. The peace of the cross firstly reconciles man to God.
      2. The peace of the cross also reconciles all things in the universe to God.
    4. How to obtain the peace of the cross
      1. Confess your own sin and your disharmony with God.
      2. Confess that Jesus died on the cross for your sins.
      3. Accept the Lord Jesus to be your Savior and your peace with God.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy-six

    SEPARATED AND ALIENATED FROM GOD

    Scripture: Col. 1:21

    1. Separated from God
      1. Man was originally created by God; he belonged to God and lived before God.
      2. Due to his sin, man was separated from God. Not only is there a barrier between man and God, but there is also a distance between the two.
    2. Alienated from God
      1. Not only is man separated from God passively, but he is also alienated from Him actively. Separation from God is a forsaking of God, but alienation is a rebellion against God. Separation is a departure from God, but alienation is an assault upon God.
      2. The life of man today is not merely one that is separated from God, but it is one that is daily antagonistic toward God. Use examples to prove this.
    3. How to be reconciled to God
      1. Confess that you are separated and alienated from God.
      2. Repent to God.
      3. Believe in Jesus Christ, the Son of God, as Savior.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy-seven

    TURNING FROM IDOLS TO GOD

    Scripture: 1 Thes. 1:9

    1. Man forsook God
      1. Man is created by God and belongs to God.
      2. Due to his sin, man forsook God.
      3. Man today is living a life of forsaking God.
    2. Man worshipped idols
      1. Sin causes man to forsake God. It also causes him to worship idols. The result of man’s sin is the worship of idols.
      2. Man worships idols because he has sinned and has lost God. God is the source of all peace and blessing. To lose God is to lose all peace and blessing. Once man lost the source of peace and blessing, he turned to idols. The more man sins, the more he loses his peace, and the more he loses his peace, the more he wants it. This psychological craving for peace and blessing turns him to idols. No one who worships idols loves them. All the idol worshippers are just trying to utilize the idols.
      3. The life of man today is a life of idol worship. Some idols are tangible; others are intangible. Whatever takes the place of God in a man is an idol. Whatever a man relies on, apart from God, is also an idol.
    3. The fallacy of idols
      1. Idols are false; hence, they are a deception.
      2. List facts to show that idols are false.
    4. The reality of God
      1. God is real and therefore trustworthy.
      2. Use examples to show how secure it is for man to trust in God.
    5. Forsake idols and turn to God
      1. Since idols are a deception, we should forsake them. Those who would not forsake them are fools. They are either deceiving themselves, or are deceiving others.
      2. Since God is trustworthy, we should turn to Him. If we do not turn to Him, we are in a deception, either deceiving ourselves or deceiving others.
    6. How to forsake idols to turn to God
      1. Recognize the fallacy of idols and the reality of God.
      2. Destroy all of the idols in your home.
      3. Repent and turn to God.
      4. Receive the Son of God, Jesus Christ, as your Savior.
      5. Worship and serve God through the Lord Jesus Christ.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy-eight

    “CHRIST JESUS CAME INTO THE WORLD
    TO SAVE SINNERS”

    Scripture: 1 Tim. 1:15

    1. Who is Christ Jesus?
      1. “Christ” signifies that He is God.
      2. “Jesus” signifies that He is man.
      3. The compound name of “Christ Jesus” means that God came as man to save men and to become the Savior of mankind.
    2. Why did Christ Jesus come into the world?
      1. Christ Jesus did not come into the world by accident or without a purpose.
      2. Christ Jesus came into the world in order to save sinners.
    3. Who are the sinners?
      1. All men are sinners. As long as you are a man in this world, you are a sinner.
      2. Christ Jesus came into this world in order to save sinners, that is, to save you. As far as I am concerned, He came to save me; as far as you are concerned, He came to save you.
    4. How can man receive the salvation of Christ Jesus?
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Seventy-nine

    THERE IS ONE GOD AND ONE MEDIATOR

    Scripture: 1 Tim. 2:5

    1. There is only one God
      1. As there cannot be two heads in a household or two kings in a nation, so there cannot be two Gods in the universe.
      2. This God is the Creator and the Ruler of the universe. He is also the Savior of mankind.
    2. There is only one mediator
      1. In human history there have been many wise and famous men, yet not one has claimed to be, nor has been recognized as, a mediator between God and man.
      2. Only Jesus Christ said that He is the mediator between God and man. The Bible says that He is the one, the only mediator.
    3. How Jesus became the mediator
      1. He was God coming as man. He had both divinity and humanity, so He was qualified to be the mediator between God and man.
      2. He was crucified and His blood was shed for our sins to remove the hindrance between God and man. So He became the mediator between God and man.
      3. He resurrected and imparted His life to man so that man could have God’s life and be one with God. Through this process He became the mediator between God and man.
    4. How to receive Jesus as your mediator
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty

    “A RANSOM FOR ALL”

    Scripture: 1 Tim. 2:6

    1. The condition of “all”
      1. This “all” refers to all men on this earth.
      2. All men have sinned, and have been condemned by God’s righteous laws. So the condition of men is that they are under the condemnation of the law.
      3. Since men are under the condemnation of the law, men are sentenced to perdition.
    2. “A ransom for all”
      1. Jesus Christ is the ransom for all. He gave Himself to become the ransom for all.
      2. Jesus is God-become-man coming to be man’s Savior.
      3. As man’s Savior, Jesus has redeemed man from the condemnation of the law and delivered him out of perdition.
      4. Jesus redeemed man by giving Himself, that is His soul-life, as a ransom.
      5. The blood Jesus shed on the cross is the ransom for all so that man may be freed from the condemnation of the law and from perdition.
    3. How to partake of Jesus’ ransom
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty-one

    GOD MANIFESTED IN THE FLESH

    Scripture: 1 Tim. 3:16

    1. The mystery of God
      1. This universe is a mystery, an unsolvable puzzle.
      2. The reason the universe is a puzzle is that its creator is mysterious.
      3. The creator of the universe is God. God is hidden, so God is mysterious.
      4. God’s being hidden does not disprove His existence. Actually, God’s being hidden serves only to prove His existence. The greater a person is, the more he is hidden. The more common a person is, the more he is seen. You see the average people on the street every day, but you hardly ever see a head of state personally. God is hidden because He is the head of the universe.
    2. God’s manifestation
      1. Anything that is in existence can be hidden, but not forever. With existence comes manifestation.
      2. An important person often manifests himself in a different form. Although he is semi-hidden or hidden in a different form, he nevertheless is manifested through it.
      3. God was manifested in such a semi-hidden way in a person called Jesus of Nazareth. When men looked upon Jesus, they saw Him as a man and as God. If you say that He is a man, He is not just a man. If you say that He is God, He also appears as a man. He is God incarnated, and He is God’s manifestation.
    3. The purpose of God’s manifestation
      1. God wants to be one with man.
      2. God created man so that man might become His container to contain God Himself.
      3. Man without God as the content is an empty and meaningless vessel.
      4. “God manifested in the flesh” means that God put on the flesh so that through that one body He might eventually be able to put Himself into thousands upon thousands of bodies. Through this process God can be one with man.
      5. Man has sinned and is separated from God. Before God can become one with man, He must accomplish redemption for man.
      6. He accomplished redemption by His death and resurrection. His death abolished man’s sins, and His resurrection imparts His life into man.
      7. When man receives His life, he is one with Him.
    4. What to do with this God
      1. Confess that you and your life are empty, without a center and without reality.
      2. Confess that God is the reality and the meaning of your living.
      3. Confess that God was incarnated in the flesh, and that He died and resurrected to accomplish redemption for us.
      4. Receive Jesus, the One who was God manifested in the flesh, as your Savior.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty-two

    “THE WASHING OF REGENERATION
    AND RENEWING OF THE HOLY SPIRIT”

    Scripture: Titus 3:5

    1. Man’s defilement
      1. Man was defiled due to the fall of Adam. This was not merely an outward defilement, but also an inward defilement of life and nature.
      2. Such a defilement of life and nature was caused by the injection of Satan’s life and nature into man.
    2. Man became old
      1. Because man’s life and nature were defiled by Satan, man became old.
      2. Because man became old, he experiences corruption, weakness, sickness, and death.
    3. The washing of regeneration
      1. Since man’s life and nature were defiled and corrupted, God’s salvation is not to change the life that man has, but to regenerate man. God regenerates man so that man may have God’s life in addition to his own life.
      2. Once God’s life gets into us, it causes us to be separated from our old life and nature. Such a separation is a kind of washing, which washes away our defiled life. So regeneration is a washing.
      3. The washing of regeneration is mainly for washing away our defiled life, not our defiled behavior.
    4. The renewing of the Holy Spirit
      1. When God saves us, He not only regenerates us so that we may receive His life, but He also puts the Holy Spirit within us so that we may receive His Spirit.
      2. The Holy Spirit is within us to renew us from our old, created, and corrupted life. God’s life is washing away our defiled life, and the Holy Spirit is renewing that same defiled and corrupted life into a new life.
      3. The renewing of the Holy Spirit is not merely to change a man’s living in an outward way. It is to renew his old nature into a new nature.
    5. How to receive the washing of regeneration and the renewing of the Holy Spirit
      1. Confess that your created life is filthy and that your nature has become old.
      2. Abhor your own life and nature.
      3. Repent and turn to God.
      4. Receive the crucified and resurrected Christ as your Savior.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty-three

    JESUS TASTED DEATH FOR MAN

    Scripture: Heb. 2:9

    1. The end man deserves
      1. The end man deserves is death.
      2. Man’s death sentence came from sin.
      3. Since man lives in sin, his end shall be death.
    2. Jesus tasted death for man
      1. Man’s death has its source in his sin. When Jesus tasted death for man, He bore man’s sin.
      2. That Jesus bore man’s sin meant that He received the punishment for sin. That punishment was death.
      3. Describe how Jesus tasted death for man, how He was forsaken by God, and how His heart melted like wax. He suffered the burning of the fire of God’s wrath. These experiences are tastes of death.
    3. The results of Jesus tasting death
      1. Man’s sins were forgiven.
      2. Man has been freed from the suffering of death.
      3. Those who believe in Him do not perish and will be resurrected if they die.
    4. How to receive the effects of Jesus’ substitutional death
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty-four

    JESUS IS ABLE TO SAVE TO THE UTTERMOST

    Scripture: Heb. 7:25

    1. Jesus is God coming as man
      1. Jesus is God coming as man to become man’s Savior.
      2. Because His power is the power of God, there is no limit to His power.
    2. Jesus’ redemption is eternal
      1. Because He is God coming as man, and God is eternal, His redemptive work on the cross is eternal.
      2. Eternal means limitless and measureless. His redemptive work has an eternal, measureless effect.
    3. Jesus is living forever
      1. Jesus not only died to accomplish redemption, but He also resurrected.
      2. Jesus not only resurrected, but now He is living forever.
    4. Jesus is always interceding
      1. Jesus died and resurrected not only to become man’s Savior, but also to become his intercessor before God.
      2. Just as His redemptive work is eternal, so also is His intercession for man.
    5. Jesus is able to save to the uttermost
      1. Jesus is God coming as man, whose redemption is eternal; He is living forever and always interceding. Thus, because He is fully qualified, He is able to save men to the uttermost.
      2. “To the uttermost” means that He is able to save men not only for all time and eternity, but also to the uttermost in extent.
    6. How to receive the salvation of Jesus
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty-five

    ETERNAL REDEMPTION

    Scripture: Heb. 9:12

    1. The need for redemption
      1. Man is sinful before God.
      2. God is righteous and so is His law. The law has a righteous requirement because of man’s sins.
      3. When man’s sin confronts God’s righteousness, there is a need for redemption.
    2. The meaning of redemption
      1. Redemption resolves man’s sins before God according to the requirement of God’s righteousness.
      2. Because of God’s righteousness, sinful men must die. So in order to redeem them, there must be another death. Only another death can satisfy the requirement of God’s righteousness, and only such a death can redeem men from their sins.
    3. The type of redemption
      1. In the time of the Old Testament, before redemption was accomplished, God set up a type of redemption.
      2. Redemption was typified by the offering of goats and bulls. Goats and bulls were killed, and blood was shed to accomplish atonement for man’s sins.
      3. The death and shed blood of goats and bulls was only a shadow, not the reality; while it made atonement for sins, it could not redeem men from their sins.
    4. The accomplishment of redemption
      1. Redemption was accomplished on the cross. The Lord Jesus bore man’s sins on the cross and suffered the punishment for sins. Thus He fulfilled the requirement of God’s righteousness and accomplished redemption for man.
      2. The redemption of the Lord Jesus is not a symbol, but a reality. The blood of goats and bulls in the Old Testament time was only a symbol, but the redemption of Christ on the cross is a real accomplished fact.
    5. The nature of redemption
      1. Redemption is eternal.
      2. “Eternal” not only refers to time, but in nature it also denotes a completion, something accomplished once for all.
      3. So Christ’s redemption, being eternal, is applicable and available to all men at any time.
    6. How to partake of Christ’s redemption
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty-six

    WITHOUT THE SHEDDING OF BLOOD,
    THERE IS NO FORGIVENESS

    Scripture: Heb. 9:22

    1. The requirement of God’s righteousness: death
    2. The significance of shedding of blood: death
    3. The meaning of shedding of blood: God’s righteous requirement is satisfied
    4. The result of shedding of blood: men’s sins are forgiven
    5. The shedding of Jesus’ blood
      1. In the Old Testament all the sacrifices were killed and their blood was shed. This was a symbol of the blood-shedding of Jesus.
      2. The shedding of Jesus’ blood signifies His death for us. The meaning of His shed blood is that God’s righteous requirement is satisfied. Thus, the effect of His blood being shed is that our sins are forgiven.
      3. Without the shed blood of Jesus, God’s righteous requirement could never have been satisfied, and man’s sins could never have been forgiven. But the shed blood of Jesus has satisfied God’s righteous requirement so that man’s sins can be forgiven.
    6. How to partake of Jesus’ blood
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty-seven

    THE PURIFYING OF THE CONSCIENCE
    BY THE BLOOD

    Scripture: Heb. 9:14

    1. The function of the conscience
      1. God is the ruler of the universe, so He is also the ruler of man.
      2. God rules man by means of man’s conscience. So in function, the conscience represents God to rule man.
      3. Whatever is condemned by the conscience is also condemned by God.
    2. The function of the blood
      1. God’s righteousness causes God to condemn man; however, Christ bore man’s sins and died for man, thus satisfying God’s righteous requirement.
      2. In the sight of God, the blood of Jesus cleansed man from sin, thereby abolishing God’s condemnation of man.
    3. The purifying of the conscience by the blood
      1. As Jesus’ blood has cleansed man from sin in God’s sight and has abolished God’s condemnation of man, so it has also taken away the condemnation of man’s conscience.
      2. By Jesus’ blood taking away the condemnation of man’s conscience, man’s conscience is purified so that there is no longer the feeling of shortcoming in the conscience.
      3. The purifying of the conscience with its feeling causes man’s conscience to be at peace before God.
    4. The result
      As the blood of the Lord Jesus cleanses man’s conscience, it not only gives peace to man’s conscience, but also enables man to serve God.
    5. How to partake of this cleansing
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty-eight

    AFTER DEATH THE JUDGMENT

    Scripture: Heb. 9:27

    1. It is reserved for men once to die
      1. Men deserve death.
      2. Death came from sin.
      3. No one can escape death. Give some examples to describe how man cannot escape death.
    2. After death comes judgment
      1. Death is not the end but a beginning. Man’s life is short, and this short life is ended by death. But after death there is eternity. This eternity is ushered in by death.
      2. Whatever man does in this age will be judged in eternity. Many commit crimes and escape the punishment of the law and the shame of public opinion. Many think they will be safe from punishment once they die. But what man does cannot be resolved by his death. Actually death is not the end of all things. Everything will be judged in the coming eternity.
    3. The results of judgment
      1. There is not one who has never committed a sin in this age, so in eternity no one can escape God’s righteous judgment and condemnation.
      2. The result of condemnation is perdition.
      3. Perdition means to go to hell.
    4. The way to escape
      Give a strong conclusion on how to escape death and judgment.

    Subject One Hundred Eighty-nine

    A NEW AND LIVING WAY

    Scripture: Heb. 10:20

    1. The path of man’s living
      1. The path of man’s living is a path that is far away from God.
      2. This path is a path of committing sins.
      3. This path is also a path of going into death.
    2. God’s saving way
      1. The Lord Jesus bore man’s sins and died for man.
      2. The Lord resurrected and imparted His life into man.
    3. A new and living way
      1. God’s saving way is a way God has prepared for man. This way is through the Lord’s crucifixion, the shedding of His blood, and through His resurrection. This way enables man to come near to God.
      2. This way was never open before, so it is a new way; and this way is in Christ’s resurrection life, so it is also a living way.
      3. This way does not have the hindrance of sin; rather, it has the power of life, drawing us close to God.
      4. This way not only brings man near to God, but also allows man to be one with God. Not only can man enjoy all the blessings that God bestows upon him, but he can also enjoy God Himself.
    4. How to partake of this way
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety

    THE NECESSITY OF BELIEVING THAT GOD IS

    Scripture: Heb. 11:6

    1. God is
      1. The creation of the universe proves that God is.
      2. The order of the universe proves that God is.
      3. Man’s physical body and mentality prove that God is.
    2. God is hidden
      1. Although God exists, He is hidden.
      2. Because God is Spirit, He is hidden to materialistic man. As a result, the materialistic man cannot see or touch the Spirit.
      3. God’s honor, greatness, and holiness cause Him to hide Himself from man who is low and filthy.
    3. You must believe that God is
      1. You must believe because God is hidden.
      2. You must believe because God is Spirit and cannot be seen by man’s naked eye.
      3. You must believe because God is honorable holy, and we are low and filthy. Thus for man to touch God, there is no way other than the way of believing.
    4. The results of believing in God
      1. By believing in God you receive His life.
      2. Believing in God causes you to have the sensation of being enlightened within.
      3. Through your believing you become well-pleasing to God.
    5. How to believe
      1. Confess that you are a sinner before God.
      2. Repent and come forward to God, believing that He is.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety-one

    JESUS IS UNCHANGING

    Scripture: Heb. 13:8

    1. Jesus is God
      1. Prove that Jesus is God.
      2. As God is eternal and unchanging, so Jesus is unchanging.
    2. Jesus is eternal
      1. Jesus died and rose again.
      2. Jesus lives today and will be living forever.
      3. What Jesus did in the past He is doing today, and in the future He will still be doing the same.
      4. Likewise, what Jesus was able to do in the past He is able to do now, and will still be able to do in eternity.
    3. Jesus is real
      1. As Jesus was so real to people when He was on the earth, so He is also real to men today.
      2. Jesus is real because He is living. Because Jesus is living forever, He will be real forever.
      3. Since Jesus is real, the deliverance and healing He gives to us is real.
    4. How to partake of this unchanging Jesus
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety-two

    THE PRECIOUS BLOOD OF CHRIST

    Scripture: 1 Pet. 1:18-20

    1. Man’s indebtedness before God
      1. Man is sinful.
      2. God is righteous.
      3. For man and God to be reconciled, the price of redemption must be paid.
    2. The blood of Christ
      1. As the indebtedness encumbered upon man must meet the requirement of God’s righteousness, it is the highest possible indebtedness.
      2. Because the highest price is demanded, nothing of man can pay it, not even man’s good works, man’s own righteousness, man’s morality, or good behavior.
      3. Only the blood of Christ can fulfill God’s requirement, so Christ’s blood becomes the only acceptable payment. This is why Christ’s blood is the precious blood. The word “precious” indicates the unique value of the blood of Christ.
      4. Christ’s blood is the precious blood not only because of its high value, but also because of His supreme nature. His blood is not like the blood of goats or bullocks; that is, the blood of the created lives. His blood is the blood which the Creator shed for His creatures.
      5. Since His blood possesses such a supreme nature and unique value, its effectiveness is unlimited.
    3. The function of the precious blood
      1. It enables man to have his sins forgiven.
      2. It enables man to be justified.
      3. It cleanses man’s conscience.
      4. It reconciles man to God.
      5. It enables man to obtain God’s life.
    4. How to partake of the precious blood of Christ
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety-three

    JESUS BORE OUR SINS

    Scripture: Gal. 3:13b; 1 Pet. 2:24

    1. Jesus was hanged upon the tree
      1. Jesus was hanged upon the tree; that is, Jesus was crucified on the cross.
      2. Crucifixion was a death penalty during the days of the Roman Empire.
      3. When Jesus was crucified on the cross, He was suffering the death penalty.
    2. Jesus Himself bore our sins
      1. Jesus suffered the death penalty not because He was sinful, but because He bore our sins.
      2. As Jesus was dying on the cross, God put all our sins upon Him. Jesus’ crucifixion was the way ordained by God to deal with our sins.
      3. During Jesus’ crucifixion on the cross, the heavens and the earth were darkened. This signifies that Jesus was forsaken by God when He bore our sins upon the cross.
    3. The results of Jesus’ bearing our sins
      1. Now we can have our sins forgiven
      2. Now we can be justified by God.
      3. Now we can obtain the life of God.
    4. How to partake of the sin-bearing Jesus
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety-four

    DEAD UNTO SINS AND
    LIVING UNTO RIGHTEOUSNESS

    Scripture: 1 Pet. 2:24

    1. Living unto sins and dead unto righteousness
      1. The real condition of man is that man is living unto sins and dead unto righteousness. When you mention a crime, everyone is living. But when you talk about righteousness, everyone is dead.
      2. Give examples to prove that man has the instinct to commit sins. For instance, a child does not need to be taught to lie.
      3. Also give examples to prove that in doing good works man is as weak and impotent as a dead person.
    2. God’s saving way
      1. We are incurable. The nature of our life is prone to sin and cannot work righteousness.
      2. Yet, in God’s regeneration, we receive His life in addition to our original life.
      3. When God’s life gets into us, we are born again and our old life is replaced by a new life.
    3. Dead unto sins and living unto righteousness
      1. As soon as God’s life enters into man, man is dead unto sins and living unto righteousness.
      2. Give examples to prove that a man is dead unto sins as soon as he is saved. Point out that formerly he was proud in committing sins, but now he is not.
      3. Then give examples to illustrate a man living unto righteousness. Point out that now he is lively and full of strength in doing good and working righteousness.
    4. How to have such a change
      1. Confess that you are weak and incapable of doing good, and that all you can do is commit sins.
      2. Repent, turn to God, and receive God’s life into you.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety-five

    THE RIGHTEOUS ONE SUBSTITUTED
    FOR THE UNRIGHTEOUS ONES

    Scripture: 1 Pet. 3:18

    1. Jesus is the righteous One
      1. Jesus is God coming as man.
      2. Jesus was born in holiness without the nature of sin.
      3. Jesus has never committed sin. Once He asked publicly, “Who among you can prove that I have sinned?” When He was examined before His crucifixion, no one could find sin in Him.
      4. Jesus is the sinless and the righteous One.
    2. We are the unrighteous ones
      1. We are sinners.
      2. We were born in sin.
      3. We have committed sins and grew up in sin.
      4. We are altogether, one hundred percent sinners.
    3. The righteous One substituted for the unrighteous ones
      1. The righteous One substituted Himself for the unrighteous ones; that is, the Lord Jesus substituted Himself for us.
      2. On the cross the Lord Jesus became our substitute by bearing our sins, shedding His blood, and dying for us.
      3. Because He bore our sins and died for us on the cross, our sins are forgiven before God. Because He died for us, we can be delivered from death and can obtain eternal life.
    4. How to partake of Jesus’ substitution
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety-six

    THE LORD’S BLOOD CLEANSES US FROM SIN

    Scripture: 1 John 1:7

    1. The Lord Jesus bore our sins on the cross and shed His blood for us
    2. The function of the Lord’s blood
      1. Because Jesus bore our sins and shed His blood, His blood can cleanse us from our sins.
      2. The cleansing of the Lord’s blood is always effective.
    3. The meaning of being cleansed from sins
      1. The Lord’s blood cleanses us from our sins; that is, it erases our record of sins before God.
      2. When we are cleansed by the Lord’s blood, all record of our sins is erased before God.
    4. How to obtain the cleansing of the Lord’s blood
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety-seven

    GOD’S FORGIVENESS AND CLEANSING

    Scripture: 1 John 1:9

    1. God’s forgiveness
      1. God’s forgiveness is based upon the redemption of the Lord Jesus.
      2. God’s forgiveness removes our record of sins.
    2. God’s cleansing
      1. God’s cleansing is by the blood of the Lord Jesus.
      2. God’s cleansing washes us from every sin. Forgiveness erases the record of sin. Cleansing removes the stain of sin.
    3. The basis of God’s forgiveness and cleansing
      1. God’s forgiveness and cleansing are based upon God’s faithfulness. God’s faithfulness is according to God’s Word. God’s Word in the Bible promises us that He will forgive us and cleanse us. When we believe in Jesus, He is bound by the faithfulness of His Word to forgive and cleanse us.
      2. God’s forgiveness and cleansing are based upon God’s righteousness. God’s righteousness is according to God’s work. The redeeming death of the Lord Jesus, which dealt with our sins, is God’s work. Today when we believe in the Lord Jesus, God is bound by His righteousness to forgive us and to cleanse us.
    4. The extent of God’s forgiveness and cleansing
      1. He cleanses us from all our unrighteousness.
      2. He forgives and cleanses the sins of all believers.
    5. How to obtain God’s forgiveness and cleansing
      1. Repent and confess your sins to God.
      2. Receive the Lord Jesus and His redemption.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety-eight

    JESUS IS THE PROPITIATION FOR OUR SINS

    Scripture: 1 John 2:2; 4:10

    1. Sin separates man from God
      1. Man’s sins violate God’s righteousness.
      2. God’s heart draws Him toward man in love, but God’s righteousness has forced Him to forsake man. Therefore, His love cannot reach sinful man.
    2. The Lord Jesus propitiates for us
      1. The Lord Jesus bore man’s sins according to the requirements of God’s righteousness.
      2. The Lord Jesus propitiated the very matter which formerly prevented God’s love from reaching man.
    3. God provides in love
      1. The Lord Jesus as our propitiation is the provision of God’s love.
      2. Because God, in His love, wants to be gracious to man while at the same time God’s righteousness puts requirements upon man, God provided man with the Lord Jesus as the propitiation.
      Note:The point is not that God was angry and would not forgive man, and that the Lord came to propitiate God’s wrath. We have to be clear. The One who conciliates the situation is God Himself. God’s heart causes Him to deal with man in love, but God’s righteousness puts requirements upon man. Therefore God Himself provided man with the Lord Jesus as the propitiation to propitiate the contradictory situation between God’s love and God’s righteousness.
    4. How to obtain the propitiation of the Lord Jesus
      Develop this point.

    Subject One Hundred Ninety-nine

    GOD IS LIGHT AND GOD IS LOVE

    Scripture: 1 John 1:5; 4:8

    1. God is light
      1. Light is a matter of nature.
      2. Light has the function of shining.
      3. God as light denotes the function of that nature of God which is shining.
      4. Once man touches God, he receives light. He is no more in darkness.
    2. God is love
      1. Love is a matter of sentiment.
      2. Love has the function of imparting warmth.
      3. God as love denotes the function of the sentiment of God which imparts warmth.
      4. Once man touches God, he receives warmth and departs from coldness.
    3. How God is expressed as light and love
      1. He shows forth His light in His Son Jesus.
      2. He shows forth His love through the cross.
      3. God caused His Son to accomplish redemption through the cross to become man’s Savior, that man may obtain Him as light and love.
    4. How to obtain God as light and love
      1. Confess that you are in darkness and in coldness.
      2. Receive the Son of God, Jesus Christ, as your Savior.
      3. Have fellowship with God through Christ.

    Subject Two Hundred

    HE THAT HAS THE SON HAS LIFE

    Scripture: 1 John 5:11-13

    1. The Son of God is God in another form
      1. The Son of God is Jesus Christ. Jesus Christ is God come as a man in order to save man.
      2. The Son of God is God made manifest to man.
    2. God’s life is in the Son of God
      1. God is in His Son, so God’s life is also in the Son.
      2. The life that is in the Son of God is the eternal life.
    3. He that has the Son of God has life
      1. Life is within the Son of God. If man wants to obtain life, he must receive the Son of God.
      2. Once man receives the Son of God, he has God and also the life of God.
    4. The proof of having life
      1. 1 John 5:12 says, “He that hath the Son hath the life.”
      2. The proof that someone has obtained life is that his living has changed. Describe how once a man receives the Lord, his life is changed.
    5. How to obtain the Son of God
      1. Confess that you do not have God’s life.
      2. Believe in the Son of God.
      3. To believe means to receive the Son of God as Savior with our heart and our spirit.

    Subject Two Hundred One

    KNOWING THAT YOU HAVE ETERNAL LIFE

    Scripture: 1 John 5:12, 13

    1. The meaning of eternal life
      1. Eternal life is life that is eternal.
      2. Eternal life is God’s life.
    2. Eternal life is in the Son of God
      1. God put His eternal life into His Son.
      2. He that has the Son of God has eternal life.
    3. The proof of having eternal life
      1. You can know whether you have eternal life. Emphasize that it is wrong if one does not know whether he has eternal life.
      2. The words of the Bible prove that we have eternal life. Here it says, “These things have I written unto you, that ye may know that ye have eternal life...”
      3. Based upon the words of the Bible, one should know that he has eternal life.
      4. If one does not believe in God’s word, he makes God a liar.
      5. We should reject our own feeling rather than disbelieve the words of the Bible; we should distrust ourselves rather than make God a liar.

    Subject Two Hundred Two

    THE WHOLE WORLD LIETH IN THE EVIL ONE

    Scripture: 1 John 5:19

    1. Men are captives of the evil one
      1. Once men followed the evil one to commit sin, they became captives of the evil one.
      2. As soon as a man is born, he is in the position of a captive.
    2. Men are in the power of the Devil
      1. To say that man became the Devil’s captive means that man fell into the power of the Devil.
      2. To be in the power of the Devil is to be dominated by him.
    3. Men are lying in the hands of the evil one
      1. Men are not only dominated by the Devil, but they are also manipulated by him.
      2. To be dominated means that one is refused his freedom; even worse, to be manipulated means one is led to act unwittingly, with no consciousness of being manipulated.
      3. To dominate is to deny one the freedom to do anything; to manipulate is to make one do something without the realization of what he is doing. A man lying in the hands of the Devil is like a patient on the operating table who, having been anesthetized, allows the doctor to operate freely.
      4. Give examples to show how man is in the Devil’s hand, committing sin without consciousness and without self-control.
    4. How to escape from the hands of the Devil
      1. Confess that you are in the hands of the Devil.
      2. Believe in Jesus as your Savior because He has destroyed the Devil and nullified the works of the Devil.

    Subject Two Hundred Three

    THE LAMB THAT WAS SLAIN

    Scripture: Rev. 5:6, 9; 1:5; 7:14, 17; 13:8

    1. The Lamb is Christ
      1. Christ came to redeem men.
      2. Christ’s redemption was accomplished through His coming as the Lamb of God. As the Lamb He was slain and His blood was shed for men.
    2. To be slain is to be crucified
      1. Christ was crucified on the cross because He bore man’s sins.
      2. Christ was crucified to satisfy God’s righteous requirement.
    3. The effectiveness of the Lamb’s being slain
      1. It enables us to depart from sins.
      2. It washes us clean and white.
      3. It qualifies us to receive the life of God.
    4. How to obtain the Lamb that was slain
      1. Confess that He was slain for you.
      2. Receive Him as your Savior.

    Subject Two Hundred Four

    THE WRATH OF THE LAMB

    Scripture: Rev. 6:12-17

    1. The Lamb is Christ
      1. The Lamb symbolizes Christ as man’s Savior Who accomplished redemption.
      2. Whenever the Bible refers to Christ as the Lamb, it alludes to His being the Savior for the redemption of man.
    2. The tender love of the Lamb
      1. Whenever the Bible mentions the Lamb, there is the thought of tender love conveyed.
      2. The way Christ appears as the Lamb is also tender-loving.
      3. When Christ was being offered up for the redemption of man, He was like a lamb being led to the slaughter; He was without murmuring or hatred.
      4. When Christ bore man’s sins on the cross, He was the Lamb full of tender love.
    3. The wrath of the Lamb
      1. While the Lamb was tender-loving for the redemption of man, Revelation 6 refers to the wrath of the Lamb.
      2. The wrath of the Lamb is not caused by man’s sins, but by man’s unbelief and rejection. Even though man is sinful, God is able to redeem him; but man’s unbelief and rejection kindle God’s wrath.
    4. The time of the wrath of the Lamb
      1. The time of His wrath will be at the end of this age.
      2. There is the possibility that the age could end at any moment.
    5. The consequence of the wrath of the Lamb
      1. When the Lamb is wroth, the heavens and the earth will be turned upside down and men will be struck with sudden terror and fear.
      2. All those who heard the gospel and did not believe, but rather rejected Him, will be in that calamity.
    6. How to escape the wrath of the Lamb
      1. Do not put off confronting God until tomorrow. Tomorrow may be the day of His wrath. Repent and believe in Him today.
      2. Today you can receive Him as the loving Lamb. Confess that He is your Savior and open your heart to Him.

    Subject Two Hundred Five

    THE ETERNAL JUDGMENT

    Scripture: Rev. 20:11-15

    1. The conclusion of the last days
      1. The last days of the universe will be concluded by judgment.
      2. Of all God’s judgments the greatest will be His judgment upon men of all generations at the end of the present heavens and earth.
    2. God’s judgment
      1. God’s judgment at the end of the present heavens and earth will be executed at the great white throne. Whiteness signifies righteousness and purity. All of man’s unrighteousness and filthiness will be reflected in front of that throne of judgment.
      2. God’s judgment will be based upon the books before Him. These are the records of all of men’s words and deeds. God’s judgment will be made according to these records.
      3. God’s judgment in that day will be made according to what we do today.
    3. The result of God’s judgment
      1. All those whose names are not written in the book of life will be cast into the lake of fire.
      2. All those whose names are written in the book of life are the ones who have believed in the Lord Jesus and have obtained His life.
      3. The result of the judgment is that all those who did not believe in the Lord Jesus will be cast into the lake of fire.
      4. To be cast into the lake of fire is to perish forever.
    4. How to avoid the eternal judgment
      1. Repent and turn to God.
      2. Receive the Lord Jesus as our Savior. This is also to obtain God’s life so that our names may be written in the book of life. Only those whose names are written in the book of life can escape the eternal judgment.

    Subject Two Hundred Six

    THE WATER OF THE FOUNTAIN OF LIFE

    Scripture: Rev. 7:17; 21:6; 22:1, 17

    1. The fountain of life
      1. God is the fountain of life.
      2. This fountain issues from the Son of God. God is in His Son Jesus Christ as the fountain of life.
    2. The water of the fountain of life
      1. The water of the fountain of life is the life of God.
      2. This water of life is flowing out of God’s Son to be received by man.
    3. The function of the water of life
      1. As water is for quenching thirst, so also is the water of life. It quenches the thirst of human living.
      2. Water is not only for quenching thirst, but also for enjoyment. So also is the water of life to man. It not only quenches man’s thirst, but also gives man eternal enjoyment.
      3. The water of life also delivers man from death.
    4. How to obtain the water of life
      1. To obtain water you must drink.
      2. You do not need to pay any price because it is freely given by God. Everyone can drink freely.
      3. To drink freely is not to depend on your works, but simply to believe and receive.

    Subject Two Hundred Seven

    THE TORMENT OF HELL

    Scripture: Rev. 14:9-11; 21:8; Mark 9:43, 48

    1. Hell is the portion of God’s wrath
      (In Rev. 14:10 cup means portion.)
      1. Because of God’s love toward man, He accomplished redemption for him.
      2. If a man refuses to repent, he remains under God’s wrath.
      3. The totality of God’s wrath is hell.
    2. There is fire and brimstone in hell
      1. Fire burns man.
      2. Brimstone chokes man.
      3. The lake of fire which burns with brimstone is unquenchable.
    3. There are worms that do not die in hell
      To be bitten by mosquitoes, bugs, or fleas is already unbearable, but imagine the torment from the worms in hell which do not die with the unquenchable fire!
    4. How to escape hell
      Develop this point.

    Subject Two Hundred Eight

    WHO SHALL BE IN THE LAKE OF FIRE

    Scripture: Rev. 21:8

    1. Those who will be in the lake of fire
      1. The fearful. These want to believe in Jesus but are afraid of others’ mocking.
      2. The unbelieving. These would not receive the Lord Jesus as their Savior.
      3. The abominable. These do not believe in the true God, but rather worship idols. This is like an evil woman who loves another man besides her own husband and commits abominations.
      4. The murderers. Once a man worships idols, it is easy for him to commit sins and to hate and kill others.
      5. The fornicators. Today’s newspapers, magazines, and movies are full of fornication.
      6. The sorcerers. These include fortune-tellers, soothsayers, astrologists, etc.
      7. The idolaters. Abomination and idolatry are nearly the same. The difference is that abomination refers to the nature of idol worship, whereas idolatry refers to the act of idol worship.
      8. The liars.
      9. All men are at least one of these eight kinds of people. Whoever is none of these, please raise your hand.
    2. How to escape the lake of fire
      1. Repent.
      2. Believe in Jesus.

    Subject Two Hundred Nine

    THE PLEASURES OF THE NEW JERUSALEM

    Scripture: Rev. 21:10; 22:5; 7:15-17

    1. The New Jerusalem is a shining city (Rev. 21:21, 18; 4:3)
      1. The street is pure gold signifying God’s divine nature.
      2. The gates are pearls signifying our entrance into the city through Christ’s redemption.
      3. The wall is jasper signifying the riches of the divine life in the believers.
    2. The New Jerusalem is God’s dwelling place
      1. There is the throne of God and of the Lamb (Rev. 22:1).
      2. There is the glory of God shining through the Lord Jesus as the lamp (Rev. 21:23).
    3. The New Jerusalem is full of the enjoyment of the blessing of life
      1. There is the tree of life (Rev. 22:2).
      2. There is the water of life (Rev. 22:1).
    4. The New Jerusalem is where God’s eternal care is manifested
      1. God’s light will shine over it.
      2. Christ will be shepherding there.
    5. In the New Jerusalem there is no more hunger, thirst, tears, darkness, or suffering
      1. There will be no hunger or thirst (Rev. 7:16).
      2. There will be no darkness (Rev. 22:5).
      3. There will be no tears (Rev. 21:4).
      4. There will be no suffering (Rev. 21:4).
    6. How to enter into the New Jerusalem
      1. Repent and believe in the Lord Jesus.
      2. Through believing, your name will be written in the Lamb’s book of life. Only those whose names are written in the book of life can enter into the New Jerusalem (Rev. 21:27).

    Subject Two Hundred Ten

    WHO WILL BE IN THE NEW JERUSALEM

    Scripture: Rev. 21:27

    1. Who will be in the New Jerusalem?
      1. Those who repent and believe in Jesus.
      2. Those who receive the Lord Jesus as their Savior.
      3. Those whose sins are forgiven.
      4. Those who have obtained God’s life.
      5. Those whose names are written in the book of life.
      6. Those who follow the Lamb.
    2. How to enter into the New Jerusalem
      Develop this point.

    Part III—Special Topics
    In the following outlines there are eight groups,
    each consisting of several topics which are suitable
    for special gospel preaching meetings.

    GROUP 1
    MATTERS RELATED TO MAN

    Subject Two Hundred Eleven

    THE ORIGIN OF MAN

    Scripture: Acts 17:24-29
    The main purpose of this subject is to prove that God exists.

    1. Man’s origin is God, because man is created by God
    2. The amazing structure of man’s body proves that man is created by God
      In passing, argue against and show the absurdity of the theory of evolution.
    3. The chemical composition of the human body proves that man is created by God
      1. The Bible says that man is made of dust, and the chemical composition of the human body is the same as dust.
      2. When you are speaking, mention in detail the function of different members of the human body, how they are utterly marvelous and could never have come about through mere evolution.
    4. Therefore, we must conclude that if there is man, there is God
      If you and I exist, there is God. Man’s existence proves that God exists.

    Subject Two Hundred Twelve

    THE NATURE OF MAN

    Scripture: Jer. 17:9; Mark 7:21-23; Rom. 7:14, 18; Gen. 8:21

    1. The characteristics of man express the nature of man
      Every object has its own characteristics. Because man is living, his characteristics express his nature. What an object is depends on its characteristics; what man is depends on his nature. In other words, with an inanimate object it is a matter of characteristics, while with a living person it is a matter of nature. If we want to study the subject of man, we cannot avoid studying the nature of man.
    2. Man’s nature, is it good or bad, virtuous or evil?
      1. First, discuss what the sages of both the East and the West have had to say. Some have said that the nature of man is good while others have said it is evil.
      2. Then, using the Bible, prove that human nature is evil. When speaking of the evil nature of man, you should mention that the nature of man at the time of creation was good (Eccl. 7:29); but later, because sin came in causing man to fall, man’s nature became evil. The evil nature came from Satan. Satan defiled and overcame man’s good nature. So, we may say that today man’s nature is evil. Use the words of the Bible to show this clearly.
    3. Conclusion
      1. Man’s nature is evil beyond repair.
      2. Man needs another life with another nature.

    Subject Two Hundred Thirteen

    THE DEEDS OF MAN

    Scripture: Rom. 3:10-18

    1. Man’s deeds express his nature
      1. What man does is a result of what he is; what he is is based upon his human nature. Since man’s nature is evil, so his deeds also are evil.
      2. Being in such a condition, man needs to realize that he is a sinner.
        In speaking of man’s evil deeds, focus upon the sins mentioned in Romans, plus some others. By this, you should touch people’s feeling and cause them to realize that they are sinners. Pick out a few sins such as lying, stealing, and adultery, discussing them thoroughly and severely. First talk about the principle, then illustrate by examples. Do not touch the deeds of man superficially, but rather dig out the sins that are within him. Depict man’s condition when he commits sins; do this in such a way that the audience may have the feeling of sin and be convicted.
    2. How to be saved from sins
      Develop this point.

    Subject Two Hundred Fourteen

    THE NEED OF MAN

    Scripture: John 3:3; Jer. 13:23; Heb. 9:22

    1. Man’s need is based upon his condition
      Because man’s nature is evil and his behavior is corrupted, there is the need to deal with his evil nature and evil deeds.
    2. Man’s self-improvement and good behavior
      1. Sages and human philosophers throughout the generations have discovered the corrupt situation of man and have often tried their best to help it. The result is that man either tries to correct himself or to do good.
      2. To try to improve oneself is an attempt to make up for the lack in one’s nature. To do good is to try to make up for the failure in one’s deeds.
    3. Man’s self-improvement and good behavior are both useless
      1. Self-improvement cannot change the evil nature of man, just as the leopard cannot change his spots and the Ethiopian cannot change his skin.
      2. The principle of man’s living by good behavior is basically wrong. Because to do good is a fundamental duty or responsibility of a human being, it cannot be regarded as an accomplishment even if a man were to succeed in doing good. Moreover, neither could good behavior hide the sins which may have been committed previously. For example, it is futile if by doing good a man attempts to erase his sin of having murdered somebody.
    4. Man needs a saving way which includes two aspects
      1. Man’s evil deeds need to be erased. Man needs a salvation whereby his sins may be taken away and the record of them may be erased.
      2. Man’s evil nature must be replaced. Because his evil nature cannot be corrected or improved, it must be replaced.
    5. God’s way of salvation
      1. The Lord Jesus shed His blood for us and ransomed us from sin. Thus, God’s salvation takes care of man’s evil deeds.
      2. Through this salvation we are regenerated and receive a new life, God’s life, which replaces the original evil nature. Such a salvation also takes care of man’s evil nature.

    Subject Two Hundred Fifteen

    THE SAVIOR OF MAN

    Scripture: Acts 4:12; 1 Tim. 1:15; Luke 2:10-11; 19:10

    1. Man needs a Savior
      Since man needs the way of salvation (refer to Subject 214), man needs a savior. There must be a savior in order that the way of salvation might be accomplished.
    2. The Lord Jesus is not a teacher but a Savior
      1. Throughout all the generations not one sage, philosopher, or religious person could call himself the Savior. At most, such people have been merely religious leaders or teachers.
      2. Only the Lord Jesus Christ called Himself the Savior. The Bible declares that He is the Savior, and also myriads of Christians throughout the generations testify that He is the Savior. Emphasize this point.
    3. He is able to save
      1. The Lord Jesus is God becoming man to be our Savior.
      2. Since He is God, nothing is impossible with Him. He can both redeem man and deliver him from sin.

    Subject Two Hundred Sixteen

    THE SALVATION OF MAN

    Scripture: Matt. 20:28; 1 Pet. 2:24; John 12:24; 1 Pet. 1:3
    The subject of this message is the cross.

    1. Since a savior is one who saves man, he must accomplish redemption for man
    2. Throughout the generations no sage, human philosopher, or religious leader has ever claimed to have accomplished redemption for man
    3. The Savior is Jesus
      1. Jesus Himself said that He would accomplish redemption for man, give up His life for man, and be a ransom for man.
      2. Stress the cross in this section.He hung upon the cross in order to bear our sins. The cross is the way of salvation which God prepared for man. When Jesus was on the cross, God put upon Him the sins of all men.
      3. The Savior not only said that He would give up His life to be a ransom for man, but also that His death would release His life. Because of His resurrection, man is able to obtain His life and be born again.
    4. Christ’s crucifixion, the shedding of His blood, and His death and resurrection are our salvation
      1. Christ’s blood takes care of our sinful deeds.
      2. Christ’s life takes care of our sinful nature.

    Subject Two Hundred Seventeen

    THE WAY OF SALVATION FOR MAN

    Scripture: Acts 2:37, 38; 16:30, 31; 10:43; John 3:36; 1:12; 6:51; 4:14; Rom. 10:8-10, 13

    1. Both the Savior and His salvation are available
    2. The need is for man to receive
      1. If a man is to receive the Savior and be saved, he must confess that his nature is corrupt and his deeds are evil. He must repent. To repent is to turn one’s thoughts and intents to God; this includes hating, confessing, forsaking, and departing from one’s sins.
      2. Once a man repents, the following step is to believe in the Lord Jesus.
        1. Believing cannot be inherited. Do not think that you are saved because your father or grandfather are pastors or elders.
        2. Believing is not joining a religion or going through a baptismal ceremony.
        3. Believing is not believing some doctrine.
        4. Believing is more than agreeing.
        5. Believing is not merely to acknowledge. To acknowledge that Jesus is the Savior crucified for us is still not enough.
        6. Believing is receiving. To receive is to eat and to drink. The Bible invites man to receive Christ by eating and drinking Him as the bread of life and the water of life. The Bible likens God’s salvation to a feast. At a feast you must use your own mouth to eat and drink in order to receive the food. Others cannot believe for you. If three generations of your forefathers believed in the Lord, or even if you yourself have been baptized and believe some doctrines, you are still not saved. You must let the Lord Jesus come into you. Merely agreeing and acknowledging are both useless. Eating and drinking the Lord Jesus as your bread and water will bring salvation to you.
    3. How to receive
      1. Call upon the Lord Jesus.
      2. Pray to Him according to the inner feeling. Do not compose a prayer. If you feel sinful within, just confess your sin-fulness; if you are conscious of a certain sin, then confess that sin.

    Subject Two Hundred Eighteen

    THE PROOF OF MAN’S SALVATION

    Scripture: 1 John 5:12-13; John 6:47; 3:18; Acts 10:43; 1 John 3:14

    1. You can know that you are saved
      Every man is aware of it when he receives something important. The Savior and His salvation are exceedingly great. When a man is saved, he must not be unaware of it. It is not right for him to receive the Savior and His salvation without realizing it.
    2. How can you know that you are saved? In other words, what proof is there that you are saved? There are two sides to the proof
      1. One side is God’s Word. God’s Word proves that you are saved.
